# Oxford Vocabulary Release Plan

Этот документ является release-specific source of truth для контура Oxford 3000 / Oxford 5000 English vocabulary course.

Статус: `final_delivery_ready_google_sheets_uploaded` для всех завершенных Oxford 3000 Core частей through B2 Part 002 and all Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension parts: B2 Parts 001-003 and C1 Parts 001-005 (`oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_001_300_v1`, `oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_002_300_v1`, `oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_003_300_v1`, `oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_004_300_v1`, `oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_005_97_v1`). Oxford 3000 Core is complete through B2 Part 002. Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension is complete and final/readback verified; on 2026-06-06 the completed package was additionally repackaged into 35 user-facing 150-word release pairs / 70 native Google Sheets, all readback verified, and on 2026-06-08 the 150-workbook metadata/quality audit blockers were repaired or policy-resolved. The 150-word resplit manifest is `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final-150/oxford_150_resplit_manifest_v1.json`; aggregate gate report `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_150_resplit_delivery_gate_v1.json` has status `pass`, 70/70 delivery manifests verified and 1,505,000 checked cells. The quality audit report `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_150_workbook_quality_audit_v1.json` is `pass` with 0 blockers. The resplit did not regenerate translations, examples or pronunciation content; it slices previously QA-passed final workbooks. Latest Oxford 5000 C1 Part 005 gate state is 30 passed / 1 warning / 0 blocked; the warning is the soft `support_language_warning_budget`, not a release blocker and not native-speaker certification. Пользователь подтвердил 2026-05-16, что Oxford нужен для product/market positioning, reported that OUP allowed the requested use, and explicitly instructed to make these releases final. On 2026-05-20 the user also explicitly approved automatic Oxford publication when a part finishes its source-package QA. Written OUP evidence is still not stored in the project; the user-reported OUP permission is accepted as a project-evidence decision for these Google Sheets deliveries. Этот документ разрешает the local Oxford source package and final US/UK Google Sheets delivery described below. It still does not authorize ordinary deck-table Postgres import, copied Oxford definitions/examples/pronunciations/audio, or claims that LunaCards is official, certified, approved or endorsed by Oxford University Press. There is no remaining uninitialized Oxford 5000 work in the current documented source-package plan.

Machine-readable contracts: `config/oxford-vocabulary-release-contract-v0.json` for Part 001, `config/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Part 002, `config/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_003_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Part 003, `config/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_004_147_v1_contract_v0.json` for Part 004, `config/oxford_3000_core_a2_part_001_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for A2 Part 001, `config/oxford_3000_core_a2_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for A2 Part 002, `config/oxford_3000_core_a2_part_003_202_v1_contract_v0.json` for A2 Part 003, `config/oxford_3000_core_b1_part_001_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for B1 Part 001, `config/oxford_3000_core_b1_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for B1 Part 002, `config/oxford_3000_core_b1_part_003_100_v1_contract_v0.json` for B1 Part 003, `config/oxford_3000_core_b2_part_001_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for B2 Part 001, `config/oxford_3000_core_b2_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for B2 Part 002, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_b2_extension_part_001_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension B2 Part 001, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_b2_extension_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension B2 Part 002, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_b2_extension_part_003_98_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension B2 Part 003, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_001_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension C1 Part 001, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_002_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension C1 Part 002, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_003_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension C1 Part 003, `config/oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_004_300_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension C1 Part 004 and `config/oxford_5000_advanced_c1_extension_part_005_97_v1_contract_v0.json` for Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension C1 Part 005.
Outbound permission request draft: `outputs/permission-requests/oxford-3000-5000-permission-request.md`.

Operational delivery rule: for Oxford 3000/5000, once source-package QA is complete, the workflow should publish automatically without asking for another delivery approval. User wording like `сохрани в Google Drive`, `сохрани в гугл диск`, `выгрузи`, `как первую часть` or `делай финальную` means the Part 001-style final delivery contour, not raw file storage. The required contour is: export two final US/UK edition `.xlsx` workbooks, upload both as native Google Sheets to the `Слова для FlashcarsLuna` folder, run Oxford Google Sheet readback, update the release contract/source-of-truth docs, and register the gate report. This standing auto-publish rule is Oxford-specific and does not authorize ordinary deck-table Postgres import or isolated Oxford DB import unless separately requested. Raw `.md`/`.csv`/`.json` Drive upload is only supporting QA evidence when the user explicitly asks to save a report/artifact/evidence file.

2026-06-06 150-word resplit final delivery checkpoint: after the full Oxford 3000/5000 package completed source-package delivery, the user asked to make the study decks smaller. `scripts/oxford/resplit-oxford-final-workbooks-150.py` rebuilds the delivery layer from the verified US/UK final workbooks into 150-row study slices without changing translations, examples, EN-US/EN-GB pronunciation content, source rows or QA decisions. `scripts/oxford/upload-and-readback-oxford-150-workbooks.mjs` uploads the generated workbooks as new native Google Sheets and runs the Oxford Google Sheet readback for each delivery manifest. Current artifacts: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final-150/oxford_150_resplit_manifest_v1.json`, `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final-150/oxford_150_upload_readback_summary_v1.json`, and gate report `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_150_resplit_delivery_gate_v1.{json,md}`. Result: 35 release pairs / 70 `.xlsx` workbooks / 70 native Google Sheets, 4,994 rows per edition, 70/70 readback verified, 1,505,000 checked cells, 0 readback errors. The previous 300-row source-package Google Sheets remain verified delivery evidence and were not deleted or overwritten. This resplit does not authorize ordinary deck-table Postgres import or isolated Oxford DB import.

2026-06-08 150-word workbook quality audit and metadata repair checkpoint: after the user asked to check all delivered decks for translation/example adequacy and metadata, a deterministic audit was added at `scripts/oxford/audit-oxford-150-workbook-quality.py` with streaming implementation `scripts/oxford/audit-oxford-150-workbook-quality-fast.py`. The initial run found metadata-only blockers: 30 Oxford 3000 A2/B1/B2 150-workbooks had `Deck Metadata.area=A1` instead of the workbook level, and Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension B2 Part 004 had two `Card Metadata.level=B1` rows (US/British) for the documented single B1 extension row folded into the B2 extension delivery. The repair is complete: `scripts/oxford/resplit-oxford-final-workbooks-150.py` version `2026-06-08.v2` writes `Deck Metadata.area` from the workbook level, and the documented B1-extension row is tracked as `documented_b1_extension_row_in_b2_extension` warning rather than a blocker. All 70 local workbooks were rebuilt, all 70 existing native Google Sheets were updated in place by `scripts/oxford/upload-and-readback-oxford-150-workbooks.mjs` using existing `google_sheet_id` / `--file-id`, and Google Sheet readback verified 70/70 delivery manifests. Current reports: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_150_workbook_quality_audit_v1.{json,md}` has `status=pass`, 70 workbooks checked, 9,988 workbook card rows checked, 0 blockers and 4,658 warnings; `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_150_resplit_delivery_gate_v1.{json,md}` has `status=pass`, 70/70 readback verified and 1,505,000 checked cells. The audit found no empty word/example cells, no exact English example fallback in non-English target languages, no known bad English-anchor examples and no script-identity blockers. Remaining warnings are exact-English word fallback/shared-form review cues in target word cells, mostly legitimate shared forms/loanwords/proper names such as `April`, `blog`, `CD`, `bank`, plus the two documented B1-extension row warnings; they are review cues, not native-speaker approval or automatic blockers. No ordinary deck-table Postgres import or isolated Oxford DB import was run.

2026-06-03 semantic-smell QA and repair checkpoint: after the user reported bad RU examples (`СПИД изменил план.`, `Решение было звуковым.`, `Решение было биологическим.`), the source rows were traced back to bad English base examples in `oxford_5000_advanced_b2_extension_part_001_300_v1` (`The AIDS changed the plan.`, `The decision was audio.`, `The decision was biological.`). The first report-only audit `scripts/audit-example-semantic-smells.mjs --sample-size=5 --seed=example-semantic-smells-all-contours-20260603 --out=outputs/qa/example_semantic_smells_all_contours_20260603.json` wrote `.json`, `.md` and `.csv` reports, checked 2,402 Oxford English example rows, 8,370 ordinary sample rows and 1,325 HSK sample rows, and proved that existing Oxford gates were insufficient for English-anchor semantic suitability. The hard repair is complete for Oxford 5000 B2 Part 001: the curated English example map was regenerated, all derived support-language examples were regenerated/repaired, EN-US/EN-GB pronunciation artifacts were rebuilt, final workbooks were re-exported, and the existing US/UK Google Sheets were updated in place and readback verified. Repaired report `outputs/qa/example_semantic_smells_all_contours_20260603_repaired.{json,md,csv}` passes with 0 Oxford release findings. `scripts/oxford/check-oxford-english-learning-gates.py` now includes hard `english_example_semantic_smell_check` for Oxford 5000 releases, and `scripts/oxford/register-oxford-gate-report.mjs` classifies it as an English-core blocker if the report is missing or has release blockers. Future Oxford 5000 parts must run an English-base semantic-fit/smell gate before support-language generation and again before final upload.

2026-06-02 new weak-source Oxford retro-audit checkpoint: after the project activated additional `source_partial` indexes for `AZ`, `SW`, `KK`, `KM`, `MY` and `NE`, `scripts/oxford/audit-oxford-new-weak-sources.mjs --languages=AZ,SW,KK,KM,MY,NE --report-only-exit-zero` was added and run against all 12 completed Oxford 3000 Core release contracts. This script is report-only: it reads completed support translation JSONL artifacts and the current `weak_dictionary_candidates.jsonl` / `weak_example_collocations.jsonl` indexes, then writes QA reports without changing contracts, workbooks, Google Sheets, Postgres or source packages. Report `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/new_weak_sources_retro_audit_az_kk_km_my_ne_sw_v1.{json,csv,md}` checked 17,994 cells and passed with 0 blockers / 7,316 advisory warnings. It scanned the expected source rows: `localdoc-azerbaijani-english-parallel-size-balanced` 121,448, `kk-en-corpora-zenodo-v1` 326,550, `seanghay-lexicon-kh-parquet` 3,126, `myanmar-open-wordnet-013-tab` 1,227, `nepali-brihat-sabdakosh-json-gz` 81,347 and `kalebu-kamusi-swahili-dictionary` 14,721. Coverage highlights are AZ 2,355/2,999 example/collocation candidate rows, KK 2,431/2,999, KM 533 dictionary candidate rows with 386 current matches, MY 473/473, NE 2,864/2,864 and SW 2,217/2,217. Missing source candidates and source-partial mismatches are not release blockers under the current Oxford policy; already final Oxford 3000 Google Sheets should not be regenerated from this audit alone. For future Oxford 5000 parts, run this source-partial retro/new-source audit as supporting QA for the affected languages alongside the existing hard Oxford gates and repair only concrete blockers or human-reviewed warning escalations.

2026-05-31 cross-part post-final spot-check and gate-hardening checkpoint: `scripts/oxford/build-oxford-post-final-language-spot-check.py --sample-size 5` was repaired and rerun against all 10 final Oxford release contracts. Version `2026-05-31.v2` samples 5 spread rows per release and checks all 54 language variants for source-package display/example cells, final US/UK workbook display/example cells and EN-US/EN-GB word/example IPA cells. It treats explicit support-language transcription exclusion markers (`false` / `not_included_for_support_language`) as compliant, accepts comma-separated IPA alternatives such as `a, an`, and reads old A1 Part 001 workbook metadata by display order where current row-review meaning ids were renamed later. Current report artifacts are `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/*_post_final_language_spot_check_v1.{json,csv,md}`. All 10 final Oxford releases pass this post-final spot check with 0 blockers. The main Oxford gate checker now includes hard `post_final_language_spot_check` and soft `support_language_warning_budget` gates. All 10 contracts were rerun and registered at 30 passed gates / 1 warning gate / 0 blocked gates; the warning is the new soft warning-budget gate, not a release blocker. A1 Part 001 local English example and EN-US/EN-GB pronunciation artifacts were identity-synced to the current row-review ids, and pronunciation display fields were resynced to the buyer-facing edition layer; English example text, IPA text/evidence, final workbook visible content and Google Sheets were not changed. Quality assessment from the same reports: hard blockers are 0; 2,150 sampled language-row entries carry 3,894 advisory warning codes, mostly `source_audit:no_source_candidate` (1,501), `example_quality:weak_language_example_review_signal` (1,200), `source_audit:weak_language_no_source_candidate` (707), `example_quality:target_example_lexical_anchor` (280), `source_audit:source_candidates_without_current_match` (179) and `source_audit:exact_english_surface_needs_loan_review` (27). These are confidence/source-evidence signals, not release blockers under the current Oxford support-language policy, and they do not equal native-speaker certification. This checkpoint is local QA evidence only; it did not re-upload or mutate Google Sheets.

No ordinary deck-table Postgres import or isolated Oxford DB import was run for this part.

2026-06-04 Oxford 5000 B2 Extension Part 002 final delivery checkpoint: `oxford_5000_advanced_b2_extension_part_002_300_v1` final delivery is complete for the next 300 rows from the Oxford 5000 extension B1/B2-filtered slice (`offset=300`, `limit=300`), source range `heal` through `stimulate`. Source package, candidate pool, source-draft workbook, release contract, row review, reviewed 300-row English example map, English examples, US/UK edition layer, EN-US/EN-GB source-backed pronunciation rows and all 52 support-language batches are complete. Support-language generation used `gemini-3.1-pro-preview` through Gemini CLI for the remaining 20 languages after the first 32 batches were cached; no paid API key was used. Source-package QA passed after weak-language targeted review, support translation sample review, all-fields sample review, source-backed support translation audit, support example quality audit and article-display check. The support example quality audit initially found 10 deterministic blockers (`RU` mosque naturalness, `MY` action-surface rows for `heal`/`invade`/`rob`, and `KM` artificial spacing for `hence`/`hopefully`/`inevitably`/`moreover`/`nowadays`/`starve`); those TSV rows were repaired, affected batches were re-registered, and the rerun support example quality audit checked 15,600 support example cells with 0 blockers. 2026-06-01 B2 Part 001 support-language workflow decision: the primary support-language draft path for B2 Part 001 and later Oxford support batches is the existing structured/local TSV contour with project scripts and Oxford gates. Gemini subscription/CLI is no longer treated as the mass generator for every language. It may be used only as a bounded reviewer/repair tool after a structured draft exists, or for small targeted review chunks when explicitly approved. Paid Gemini API generation is not part of this workflow unless the user explicitly reverses that decision. Any partial Gemini cache files under `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/gemini-support-generation/` are auxiliary evidence only: they do not count as a support-language batch, must not be registered in the release contract, and must not be delivered until a complete TSV/JSONL artifact passes the standard Oxford support-language checks. This decision keeps B2 continuation on the old structured contour while preserving Gemini as an optional second-pass quality tool.

## Current Decision

Oxford 3000 / Oxford 5000 is now a desired licensing target for LunaCards, not just a passive benchmark. The user reports that OUP allowed the requested use, and for A1 Parts 001-004 plus A2 Parts 001-003 that user-reported state is accepted as sufficient project evidence for final US/UK Google Sheets delivery. A2 Part 003 final delivery is complete under the documented Oxford standing auto-publish rule after source-package QA completion; the earlier operational Google Drive OAuth blocker was cleared by reauthorization and both native Google Sheets passed readback.

Даже after final delivery approval for this release нельзя:

- копировать Oxford definitions, examples, pronunciations or explanatory copy;
- переименовать Oxford list и считать ее оригинальным LunaCards source;
- писать в продукте `official`, `certified`, `approved`, `endorsed by Oxford` or comparable claims.

Можно вести Oxford source-package workflow and final delivery for this first release with: Oxford headword/POS/CEFR/list-membership snapshot, own `meaning_id`, own `meaning_note`, own `semantic_scene`, own examples, own QA evidence, source-assisted translation checks, final US/UK workbooks and final Google Sheets.

For the current Oxford A1 final Google Sheets releases and future Oxford parts under the standing auto-publish rule, the project-evidence decision records these allowed fields:

- Oxford 3000 headwords;
- part-of-speech labels;
- CEFR labels;
- exact list membership;
- list order or ordering bands;
- name/branding such as `Oxford 3000` / `Oxford 5000`;
- LunaCards-authored learner examples;
- 54-language support translations and examples;
- Google Sheets/workbook delivery for this release;
- downloadable/app flashcard reuse for this release.

Blocked fields remain: copied Oxford definitions, copied Oxford dictionary examples, copied Oxford pronunciation text, Oxford audio, and any claim that the LunaCards release is official/certified/approved/endorsed by Oxford University Press.

Required attribution/no-endorsement wording: `Oxford 3000 and Oxford 5000 are Oxford University Press word lists. This LunaCards workbook is independently prepared by LunaCards and is not official, certified, approved, or endorsed by Oxford University Press.`

## External Terms Snapshot

Checked on 2026-05-05 against official Oxford Learner's Dictionaries pages:

- Oxford describes the Oxford 3000 as a curated list for vocabulary learning and says the list covers British and American English.
- Oxford FAQ says the word-list pages have download/print PDF functions for offline study.
- Oxford Learner's Dictionaries Terms and Conditions reserve OUP intellectual property rights and restrict systematic printed/electronic copying, public electronic distribution, sublicensing and content reuse unless allowed by product-specific terms.

Conclusion for LunaCards: public browsing/download for study is not the same as permission to build a commercial/mass workbook source list from Oxford content. Treat Oxford 3000/5000 as benchmark only until a documented permission/licence decision says exactly what may be reused.

References:

- https://www.oxfordlearnersdictionaries.com/about/oxford3000
- https://www.oxfordlearnersdictionaries.com/us/faq/index.html
- https://www.oxfordlearnersdictionaries.com/terms-and-conditions.html
- https://academic.oup.com/pages/purchasing/rights-and-permissions

2026-05-16 request package prepared for user review/sending:

- outbound draft: `outputs/permission-requests/oxford-3000-5000-permission-request.md`;
- machine-readable contract state updated in `config/oxford-vocabulary-release-contract-v0.json`;
- Decision Log updated with the Oxford licensing target.

Request goal:

1. Confirm whether OUP can license Oxford 3000/5000 for LunaCards.
2. Confirm allowed fields and forbidden fields.
3. Confirm permitted product surfaces: Google Sheets/workbooks, web/app flashcards, downloadable files, paid/commercial distribution, 54-language translations, learner examples and source metadata.
4. Confirm exact branding/attribution/no-endorsement requirements.
5. Confirm whether a sample/pilot is allowed before full commercial launch.

Before the 2026-05-16 user-reported permission, no Oxford list snapshot, PDF extraction, scraper, copied definitions, copied examples, copied pronunciation content, or generation from Oxford data was authorized. After the 2026-05-17 final instruction, this project accepts the user-reported permission as project evidence for the first final US/UK Google Sheets delivery, while written OUP evidence remains worth storing later if received.

2026-05-16 user later reported: "все можно" and instructed to start cards. Based on that user-reported permission, the project prepared a local Oxford 3000 source package. This is an operational user-reported permission state, not stored OUP written evidence.

## Current Source Package

2026-05-16 first Oxford source package was built with `scripts/oxford/build-oxford-source-package.py`.

Command:

```bash
/Users/lali/.cache/codex-runtimes/codex-primary-runtime/dependencies/python/bin/python3 scripts/oxford/build-oxford-source-package.py --release=oxford_3000_core_a1_part_001_150_v1 --course-id=oxford_3000_core --levels=A1 --limit=150 --workbook-name=FlashcardsLuna_Oxford_3000_Core_A1_Part_001_source_draft.xlsx --main-sheet-name='Oxford 3000 Core'
```

Result:

This is a semantic plausibility sample, not native-speaker certification;

Local sources are candidate evidence only; no-source and partial-source rows remain review signals, not native-speaker approval or automatic rejection;

The opposite English variant is not present in the buyer-facing main sheet. Empty support-language transcription columns are not present. `Course Metadata` is localized across the same 53 buyer-facing language columns with `Part 1` in the title; `Card Metadata` has 28 structural columns; no ordinary deck-table Postgres import;

| Field | Draft value |
| --- | --- |

| Regional variant | `EN-GB` as British English variant; not a separate source package, but a separate buyer-facing edition export |
| Target languages | all 54 spreadsheet language columns from `config/language-order.json`; the source package keeps source/QA traceability, while the current US/UK edition exports use the Oxford English-learning workbook shell with no empty support-language transcription columns |

| Source-list role | User-reported licensed source; explicit project evidence decision accepted for this first final delivery |
| Production source candidates | NGSL, CEFR-J cross-check, internal curation, Kaikki/Wiktionary English, OMW/WordNet, Wikidata/Concepticon |
| Row identity | `release_id::core_item_id`; stable `meaning_id` remains semantic identity |
| Sense model | one source headword can produce multiple `meaning_id` rows when POS/sense/scene differs |
| Level model | internal `core_band` + internal CEFR-like `level_min`/`level_max`; CEFR labels/list membership are allowed for this final release by project-evidence decision |
| Example policy | LunaCards-authored short examples only; no Oxford examples copied |
| Pronunciation policy | EN-US pronunciation uses local CMUdict evidence; EN-GB pronunciation uses local Britfone evidence and deterministic fallbacks; Oxford pronunciation text/audio remains blocked unless explicitly licensed |
| QA posture | source-assisted, fail-closed; local sources are candidate evidence, not automatic approval |

Recommended source model: keep `EN` / US English as the canonical default source layer and add `EN-GB` as a regional override layer. Do not duplicate semantic source rows for US/UK; export two buyer-facing edition workbooks from the same reviewed source package.

## Workbook Structure

This course should use the HSK-style course workbook principle: one workbook per release, source item rows, fixed 54 language columns, and service sheets that preserve source/QA traceability.

Main sheet draft fields:

- `release_id`
- `course_id`
- `row_id`
- `core_item_id`
- `meaning_id`
- `source_language`
- `source_variant`
- `source_headword`
- `part_of_speech`
- `sense_no`
- `core_band`
- `level_min`
- `level_max`
- `benchmark_membership`
- `source_status`
- `meaning_note`
- `semantic_scene`
- translation columns in the exact order from `config/language-order.json`
- example columns in the same exact language order
- `qa_status`
- `qa_notes`

Service sheets:

- `_README`
- `_languages`
- `_source_contract`
- `_benchmark_audit`
- `_source_assisted_qa`
- `_source_decisions`
- `_release_metadata`

Target-language transcription remains out of scope for the source-package support batches. The final US/UK edition workbooks use an Oxford English-learning variant of the LunaCards spreadsheet shell: 53 buyer-facing word columns, 53 buyer-facing example columns and then exactly two primary-English IPA columns at the end of each main sheet. US main sheet uses `EN transcription` and `EN example transcription`; British main sheet uses `EN-GB transcription` and `EN-GB example transcription`. EN and EN-GB word/example transcriptions are both preserved in source-backed edition pronunciation artifacts, but each buyer-facing workbook shows only its primary English edition. The 52 support-language word-transcription columns must not be generated as empty columns for Oxford English-learning releases. Source-language pronunciation evidence for the first 150 A1 rows now exists for both buyer-facing English editions: EN-US uses local CMUdict exact-token lookup plus deterministic ARPABET-to-IPA conversion; EN-GB uses local Britfone exact-token lookup plus deterministic spacing normalization, regular-inflection fallback from exact base forms and Britfone README initialism handling. Oxford pronunciation text/audio remains blocked unless explicitly licensed.

Article/display policy for this Oxford bundle:

- English source headwords stay Oxford-style lemmas/headwords. Do not add artificial `a/an/the` to English source headwords just to teach articles.
- Support-language display translations may keep natural articles, gender markers or classifier-like markers where that language normally teaches nouns with them and where the marker helps a learner understand the English item. This belongs in the support translation display, not in the English headword.
- This article/display policy applies to the next Oxford 3000/5000 parts in the same bundle unless a later source-of-truth decision changes it.

## Edition Export Model

Decision as of 2026-05-17: do not duplicate semantic content to create separate US and UK source packages. Keep one canonical Oxford A1 source package and export two buyer-facing final editions from it.

Shared across both editions:

- `release_id`, `course_id`, `row_id`, `core_item_id`, `meaning_id`;
- `source_headword`, learner sense/POS, level fields, benchmark membership, `meaning_note` and `semantic_scene`;
- one canonical 54-variant source/QA order from `config/language-order.json`, while each buyer-facing main sheet uses only its primary English variant plus the 52 support languages: 53 word columns, 53 example columns and the final two primary-English word/example IPA columns;
- the same legal/source policy and final delivery status.

Edition-specific fields:

- `deck_id`, `deck_title`, `deck_edition`, `source_variant`, `primary_language_code`;
- primary English `display_headword`;
- primary English example;
- primary English `transcription`;
- primary English `example_transcription`;
- `pronunciation_status`, `pronunciation_source` and `variant_note`.

Current final edition workbooks:

- US English: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final/FlashcardsLuna_Oxford_3000_Core_A1_Part_001_US_English.xlsx`;
- British English: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final/FlashcardsLuna_Oxford_3000_Core_A1_Part_001_British_English.xlsx`;
- manifest: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_001_150_v1_edition_exports_final_v1.json`;
- US English Google Sheet: `https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1krmAB56Bg7xLVHhOVj7tyJU-nzTzF2lZl-NOXnc2D_Y/edit?usp=drivesdk`;
- British English Google Sheet: `https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/18TYpNhaxHqMwvpuTNIIAyvNkRPq19mkK4FNtouBpAZU/edit?usp=drivesdk`.

Each workbook has the same required sheet set as ordinary polyglot LunaCards exports: main vocabulary sheet, `Course Metadata`, `Deck Metadata`, `Card Metadata`, `_README`, `_qa_status` and `_languages`. Main sheet shape is 150 data rows x 108 columns. The main sheet contract is `53 buyer-facing word columns -> 53 buyer-facing example columns -> primary English word IPA -> primary English example IPA`. Article-language support displays include natural articles/gender markers where the native language normally teaches nouns with them; the current repair changed 948 display cells across 12 article languages and did not add support transcription columns. `Course Metadata`, `_qa_status` and `_languages` use the same 53 buyer-facing language columns as the main sheet, not both English variants. `Card Metadata` has 28 structural columns and no duplicate example-transcription columns. The US workbook is marked with `primary_language_code=EN`; the British workbook is marked with `primary_language_code=EN-GB`. Both Google Sheets were exported back and readback verified. They are not imported into ordinary deck-card tables; ordinary deck-table Postgres import remains false.

## Dedicated Oxford DB Isolation

Decision as of 2026-05-17: Oxford source-package data may be stored in Docker/Postgres only through dedicated Oxford tables. It must not be written into ordinary LunaCards deck-card tables unless a later explicit final-delivery decision creates a separate ordinary import path.

Dedicated migration:

```text
db/migrations/027_oxford_vocabulary_isolation.sql
```

Dedicated tables:

```text
oxford_vocabulary_source_items
oxford_vocabulary_edition_items
oxford_vocabulary_support_items
oxford_vocabulary_db_import_runs
```

Import command:

```bash
node scripts/oxford/import-oxford-a1-to-db.mjs
```

The importer validates artifact coverage first, then applies only migration `027`, upserts into `oxford_vocabulary_*`, checks readback hashes, checks idempotency and verifies that ordinary deck-card tables contain zero Oxford rows. It deliberately does not insert into:

```text
content_sets
meaning_units
meaning_set_memberships
meaning_examples
meaning_language_entries
meaning_example_translations
generation_batches
generation_batch_items
qa_reviews
exports
export_items
```

Current DB isolation report:

```text
outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_001_150_v1_db_isolation_import_20260517.json
```

Current readback status:

```text
status: ok
source rows: 150
edition rows: 300
support rows: 7800
US edition rows: 150
British edition rows: 150
support languages: 52
ordinary table leak count: 0
readback mismatches: 0
foreign-key blockers: 0
idempotency rerun: 150 source / 300 edition / 7800 support unchanged, 0 inserted, 0 updated
```

This is isolated source-package persistence. Final Google Sheets delivery for the US/UK edition workbooks is now approved and complete, but ordinary deck-table imports remain blocked unless a later explicit ordinary-polyglot import decision is made.

## Release Slicing

Product packaging decision as of 2026-05-16:

- User-facing product structure should be **2 courses + 1 bundle**, not 19 separate products.
- Product 1: `Oxford 3000 Core` covering A1, A2, B1 and B2.
- Product 2: `Oxford 5000 Advanced Extension` covering the additional B2/C1 words beyond Oxford 3000.
- Bundle: `Complete Oxford 3000 + 5000 Vocabulary`, which packages both courses.
- Internal production/delivery may still use smaller `parts` for QA, export, progress and manageable study chunks.
- Historical source-package production chunk size after the pilot: about 250-300 source rows per part. Current user-facing study delivery is the 2026-06-06 150-word resplit described below.
- Do not present the main UX as one 5000-row workbook. It is useful only as an optional complete archive/power-user export after modular releases are stable.
- Do not present the main UX as 19 unrelated decks. That makes navigation feel messy; levels and parts should live under the two course products.

Current parsed source counts:

| Source package | Parsed rows | Level distribution |
| --- | ---: | --- |
| Oxford 3000 | 3000 | A1 897, A2 802, B1 701, B2 600 |
| Oxford 5000 extension | 1995 | B2 697, C1 1297, one B1 row to fold into extension handling |

Later Oxford 3000 parser repairs removed PDF continuation fragments from active source-package builds. No ordinary deck-table Postgres import, isolated Oxford DB import, Google Sheets upload or final workbook export has been run for B1 Part 003.

Competitive/learner-UX rationale:

- Oxford itself frames `Oxford 3000` as core A1-B2 and `Oxford 5000` as an advanced extension that includes Oxford 3000 plus additional words.
- Competitor and community patterns commonly expose big vocabulary sources through levels, lessons, parts, tags or subdecks rather than forcing one giant learner workflow.
- Reddit/Anki discussions show a tradeoff: one huge deck is overwhelming, but too many tiny standalone decks make navigation noisy. Therefore LunaCards should sell/label two coherent courses and use internal parts for progress.

## Applicable Local Sources

Existing project sources can help, but they do not replace final review:

| Source family | Use in this contour |
| --- | --- |
| Kaikki/Wiktionary | English POS/sense candidates; target-language dictionary candidates where available. |
| DBnary | Cross-dictionary lexical candidates for many major languages. |
| FreeDict/Apertium | EN-target translation candidates and warning evidence, especially for common words. |
| PanLex vocabulary and PanLex meanings | Broad multilingual candidate pool; useful for weak-source languages, never final truth by itself. |
| Tatoeba/OPUS | Candidate natural example evidence and collocation sanity, not direct example copying without review. |
| Wikidata/Concepticon | Concept labels, multilingual aliases and concept disambiguation support. |
| Hunspell | Spelling/form sanity for supported languages. |
| OMW/WordNet | English sense support and semantic grouping candidates. |
| CC-CEDICT, JMdict, NIKL, LEXiTRON, SEAlang and weak-language dictionaries | Language-specific reference support for Chinese, Japanese, Korean, Thai/SE Asian and weaker-source languages. |
| IPA/source caches | Optional future pronunciation support; current draft does not include target-language transcription. |

These sources are useful for source-assisted preflight and QA evidence. They must not auto-promote a row to `approved`; they can only produce candidates, warnings, and evidence for review.

## QA Gates

These gates are **release-specific to Oxford / English-learning courses**. They do not replace or weaken the ordinary LunaCards polyglot deck gates in [QA Process](qa-process.md) and [Data Delivery Pipeline](data-delivery-pipeline.md). Ordinary 180-deck LunaCards releases still require the full polyglot contour: 54 final language variants, source-backed translations/transcriptions, semantic-scene QA, final export, Google Sheet readback, post-final linguistic audit and delivery freshness.

The Oxford course is not treated as a "learn any language from any language" polyglot deck. Its quality center is English learning: the English headword, learner sense, CEFR fit, example and pronunciation must be strong. Other languages, if included, are a support layer to help the learner understand the English item.

Minimum gates before any real Oxford / English-learning release:

### Source And Legal Gates

1. `source_license_review`: confirm whether exact Oxford list/levels/order can be used, or switch to open-source/internal list with Oxford benchmark-only audit.
2. `permission_evidence_or_project_evidence_decision`: store written OUP permission/licence evidence or explicitly accept the user-reported permission state as sufficient project evidence before final delivery.
3. `allowed_fields_review`: record which Oxford fields may be used: headwords, POS, CEFR labels, list membership, order bands, branding and attribution.
4. `no_oxford_content_copy_check`: block copied Oxford definitions, examples, pronunciation text, audio or explanatory copy unless explicitly licensed.
5. `attribution_no_endorsement_review`: verify required attribution and block `official`, `certified`, `approved by Oxford`, `endorsed by Oxford` or comparable claims unless explicitly allowed.

### English-Learning Core Gates

6. `source_list_snapshot`: create a versioned source candidate pool with hashes and source decisions.
7. `row_identity_check`: unique `row_id`, stable `meaning_id`, no accidental surface-only duplicates.
8. `learner_sense_pos_check`: POS and sense must map to the intended `meaning_note` and `semantic_scene`, with sense splits where one headword has multiple learner-relevant meanings.
9. `cefr_level_fit_check`: the row's `level_min` must fit the intended course level slice (`A1`, `A2`, `B1`, `B2`, `C1`) and must not promote a rare or advanced meaning into a beginner part.
10. `cefr_level_span_review`: warning gate for rows where the source row combines multiple POS/sense levels; the learner-sense review must choose the beginner-safe meaning before final delivery.
11. `learner_value_check`: the item must be useful for English learners in the course scope, not filler chosen only because it appears in the source list.
12. `english_variant_check`: `EN` is the default US English layer; `EN-GB` differences must be intentional and documented as a separate buyer-facing edition export, not a duplicate source package.
13. `english_pronunciation_source_check`: any source-language pronunciation/IPA must come from allowed documented sources such as CMUdict or another approved pronunciation source, not copied Oxford pronunciation content.
14. `english_example_quality_check`: learner-facing examples must be LunaCards-authored, short, natural, meaning-specific and grammar-light for the level.
15. `benchmark_audit`: compare coverage against Oxford benchmark without copying restricted content.

### Support-Language Gates

16. `support_language_role_check`: translations and translated examples are support aids for English learning in the source-package gate. The US/UK edition workbooks use the Oxford English-learning sheet contract; support-language word transcriptions are out of scope and empty support transcription columns are forbidden.
17. `support_translation_meaning_check`: support translations must preserve the English learner sense and avoid obvious wrong meaning, English fallback, wrong script and source conflicts.
18. `support_example_scene_check`: translated examples must preserve the English semantic scene naturally enough to support the learner.
19. `weak_language_targeted_review`: weak-source languages use one-language or very small batches and targeted source checks. The current final US/UK Google Sheets use the explicit contract decision that support-language word transcriptions are not required and empty support transcription columns are not present for this English-learning release.
20. `support_translation_sample_review`: deterministic 10-word-per-language sample review must be recorded for the current final package, including EN, EN-GB and all 52 support languages. The review must cover both sampled display translations and sampled example sentences; when final US/UK workbooks exist, it must also compare the sampled display/example cells in those workbooks against the contract-backed source artifacts. This proves a human-readable semantic spot-check and final-workbook parity for the sample, but it does not replace a full native-speaker audit.
21. `all_fields_sample_review`: deterministic 10-word-per-language all-fields sample review must be recorded before final delivery, including EN, EN-GB and all 52 support languages. The review must cover canonical row metadata, English US/GB display/example/transcription evidence, support-language display/example fields, support QA cell status and absence of target-language transcription fields. It blocks final delivery when missing, stale or blocked, but it does not replace native-speaker certification or final Google Sheet readback.
22. `support_translation_source_backed_audit`: full support-language display translations must have a release-specific source-backed audit artifact before final delivery. The audit checks every support display cell against local indexed dictionary/concept candidates, blocks deterministic script/display failures, records no-source and source-mismatch warnings, and treats local sources as candidate evidence rather than final truth or native-speaker approval.
23. `support_example_quality_audit`: full support-language examples must have a release-specific deterministic quality audit before final delivery. The audit checks every support example cell for presence, punctuation, expected script, example casing, CJK/Thai/Khmer/Lao spacing, Burmese action-surface blockers, known naturalness-shape blockers and pedagogical quality blockers. Lexical-anchor and weak-language signals remain warning evidence in this Oxford support context; they do not equal native-speaker approval.

### Workbook And Delivery Gates

24. `workbook_contract_check`: verify source-package workbook shape plus any US/UK edition workbook sheet shape, language order, metadata, statuses and release hashes.
25. `release_specific_audit_script_check`: implement and pass an Oxford/English-learning audit script before generation/import/final delivery.
26. `final_delivery_approval_check`: no ordinary deck-table Postgres import, Google Sheet delivery or learner-facing final release until the Oxford contract explicitly allows that stage. For Part 001-Part 004, the contracts now allow final US/UK Google Sheet delivery and still block ordinary deck-table Postgres import. For future Oxford parts in this same release bundle, the 2026-05-20 standing rule means source-package QA completion authorizes the final Google Sheets delivery contour without another approval prompt.
27. `post_final_language_spot_check`: after final US/UK workbook export, native Google Sheets upload and Google Sheet readback, run `scripts/oxford/build-oxford-post-final-language-spot-check.py --sample-size 5` and require a release-specific `latest_post_final_language_spot_check` artifact with `status: pass`, all 54 language variants covered, all 52 support languages covered, final workbook display/example cells checked, EN-US/EN-GB word/example IPA rows checked and `blocker_count: 0`. This is a hard final-delivery gate for future Oxford parts and for any re-registration of existing final parts.
28. `support_language_warning_budget`: after `post_final_language_spot_check` passes, count advisory warning codes from the same report. This is a soft/advisory gate: it records over-budget source-evidence, weak-language, lexical-anchor and loan-review signals as a warning gate, but does not block release unless another hard gate reports a blocker. Current thresholds are stored in `scripts/oxford/check-oxford-english-learning-gates.py` and are intentionally used for review planning, not native-speaker certification.

Executable gate checker:

```bash
/Users/lali/.cache/codex-runtimes/codex-primary-runtime/dependencies/python/bin/python3 scripts/oxford/check-oxford-english-learning-gates.py
```

## 2026-05-05 Safe Path Decision

The next workstream proceeds as `English Core 3000`, not as an Oxford-sourced course. Oxford remains `benchmark_only`; the active source-acquisition draft lives in [English Core 3000 Source Plan](english-core-3000-source-plan.md).

## 2026-05-16 Oxford Licensing Target

User confirmed: Oxford is needed for product positioning, and the next step is preparing a request to OUP. This updates the Oxford contour from passive benchmark planning to `permission_request_prepared`.

This does not override the 2026-05-05 safe path for the already delivered English Core first release. Current English Core artifacts remain NGSL/CEFR-J/internal-source based and must not be relabelled as Oxford. Any future Oxford-based release requires a separate source-list snapshot and contract update after permission.

## 2026-05-16 Oxford Source Package Started

User reported that OUP allowed the requested Oxford usage and instructed to start cards. A local source package was created from the official Oxford 3000 PDF, producing a 3000-row normalized source snapshot and, after the packaging decision, a 150-row A1-only source-draft workbook for `Oxford 3000 Core - A1 Part 001`. At that moment it was not a final card release; the missing examples/translations/QA/delivery work was completed in the 2026-05-17 final delivery step below.

## 2026-05-17 Oxford A1 Final Delivery

User explicitly instructed to make the final release. The project accepted the user-reported OUP permission as project evidence, recorded allowed fields and no-endorsement wording, generated final US English and British English edition workbooks, uploaded both to Google Sheets, verified readback by Drive export and passed the Oxford English-learning gate checker.

Final delivery outputs:

- US English Google Sheet: `https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1krmAB56Bg7xLVHhOVj7tyJU-nzTzF2lZl-NOXnc2D_Y/edit?usp=drivesdk`;
- British English Google Sheet: `https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/18TYpNhaxHqMwvpuTNIIAyvNkRPq19mkK4FNtouBpAZU/edit?usp=drivesdk`;
- final manifest: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/final/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_001_150_v1_edition_exports_final_v1.json`;
- gate report: `outputs/oxford-vocabulary/qa/oxford_3000_core_a1_part_001_150_v1_oxford_english_learning_gates_v1.md`.

This final delivery does not import Oxford rows into ordinary deck-card tables. Oxford data remains isolated in `oxford_vocabulary_*`.
